    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer11115338538505616533"><b>Who <i>hasn't</i> dreamed of going to the moon? That dream for eleven-year-old Leo Gray is about to come true—but he’s in for the surprise of his life!</b><br/><br/>In the year 2113, most people live in robotically maintained homes, ride around in self-flying cars, and wear ozone-resistant clothes.   <span id="freeText11115338538505616533" style="display:none"><b>Who <i>hasn't</i> dreamed of going to the moon? That dream for eleven-year-old Leo Gray is about to come true—but he’s in for the surprise of his life!</b><br /><br />In the year 2113, most people live in robotically maintained homes, ride around in self-flying cars, and wear ozone-resistant clothes. Most people that is; just not Leo Gray’s parents. They’re stuck in the past, and science know-it-all Leo is completely fed up with his beyond-embarrassing living arrangement with them. But when he enters a rocket-building competition for a chance to attend the Lunar Academy, Leo’s luck finally seems to turn in his favor!<br /><br /> However, it's not long after stepping foot into his dorm room that Leo discovers the Moon’s celebrated city is harboring a world of dark secrets. It's soon a race against the clock for Leo and his friends Andromeda Groves (a code-hacking whiz from Canada), Pavo Digbi (a history buff from Brazil), and Grus Pinwheel (a musically gifted and comically endearing Aussie) to intercept and foil plans to destroy the city—leaving the group’s leader faced with a decision that no eleven-year-old should ever have to make: save Earth or save himself and the city he fought so hard to reach.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2666425717" />
    <a title="Heather" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/91930007-heather"><img alt="Heather" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547328189p2/91930007.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2666425717?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/91930007-heather">Heather</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2666425717" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer626025167013370220">I received this book in exchange for a honest review. Overall I thought the plot and characters were a lot of fun and I really enjoyed how the author kept me guessing about what would happen next for Leo and his friends. I ended up reading the whole thing in just two nights because I was so curious to see how things would turn out for them! The plot is set a hundred years in the future, but Leo's family are really weird and live like it's still the modern era, which is pretty funny. Leo is your </span>
  <span id="freeText626025167013370220" style="display:none">I received this book in exchange for a honest review. Overall I thought the plot and characters were a lot of fun and I really enjoyed how the author kept me guessing about what would happen next for Leo and his friends. I ended up reading the whole thing in just two nights because I was so curious to see how things would turn out for them! The plot is set a hundred years in the future, but Leo's family are really weird and live like it's still the modern era, which is pretty funny. Leo is your typical science loving kid who enters a rocket competition to try to get to the new school inside the moon, but he instead gets grounded to helping his neighbor stop trees from disappearing in their neighborhood. Leo's neighbor tells Leo that the reason the trees are disappearing is because of aliens, but Leo doesn't believe him until he actually meets a baby one named Grimlu. Grimlu then tells Leo and his friends about a evil breed of aliens called Mleckorgs which invade planets and suck away all traces of their life, which they did a long time ago to our surrounding planets, like Mars. Earth of course, is next on their list. This sends Leo and his friends on a wild goose chase to come up with a plan to stop the Mleckorg's portal from opening on the night of the lunar eclipse. But, without revealing too much, everything you think you knew ends up being completely off when you reach the final chapter. In short, I really enjoyed reading this book. It reads like a classic middle-grade fantasy novel but with a fun sci-fi twist!</span>
  <a data-text-id="626025167013370220" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2699782356?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bryan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bryan" href="/user/show/93040992-bryan">Bryan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2699782356" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16190720179934085517">Got the ARC off a friend who's making me do this review. I first thought it was kinda slow, but it turned out to be much cooler than I was expecting. The storys about this family that live in the future but haven't adapted to modern times, so their son enters a science competition go to the new school on the moon. The main character kinda reminds me of Spidey, cause he's this really smart nerd but turns out to be something of a superhero at the end. So the plot starts with Leo trying to get to t</span>
  <span id="freeText16190720179934085517" style="display:none">Got the ARC off a friend who's making me do this review. I first thought it was kinda slow, but it turned out to be much cooler than I was expecting. The storys about this family that live in the future but haven't adapted to modern times, so their son enters a science competition go to the new school on the moon. The main character kinda reminds me of Spidey, cause he's this really smart nerd but turns out to be something of a superhero at the end. So the plot starts with Leo trying to get to the moon, he goes to space camp, then once he gets to Luna City the plot revolves around him finding a strange alien note, the moon school's library getting ransacked, and Leo's pet mouse getting lost. The lost mouse eventually leads Leo to finding a trapped baby alien who explains that Earth is going to be destroyed by an evil alien species on the night of the eclipse. Leo and his friends prematurely think they can stop it but when the alien disappears right after Leo and his friends release it, Leo finds out there was an evil alien trying to destroy the city the entire time, right under his eyes! To end, anyone who likes HP or Percy Jackson should read this book. I give it five stars because 1) I'm seventeen and still enjoyed reading it 2) the plot has a good amount of action shortly after getting into it 3) because I wasn't expecting how things turned out in the end and am actually wishing there was a sequel so that I can figure out what Leo's superpower is already!?!?!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16190720179934085517" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2713603845" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2713603845" />
    <a title="Schizanthus Nerd" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52870273-schizanthus-nerd"><img alt="Schizanthus Nerd" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588332751p2/52870273.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2713603845?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Schizanthus Nerd" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Schizanthus Nerd" href="/user/show/52870273-schizanthus-nerd">Schizanthus Nerd</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52870273-schizanthus-nerd?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52870273-schizanthus-nerd?shelf=kindle-food">kindle-food</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2713603845" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13743896112304670658">Leo Gray is embarrassed by his behind the times parents who don’t see the need for anything high-tech. They own Minutes & Widgets, a clock fixing shop, which isn’t doing so well in 2113 when most people rely on self-flying cars and robots that do all of the housework. Leo is an eleven year old science whiz who is hoping to secure a place at the Lunar Academy, located in a new city inside the moon called Luna City.<br/><br/>Leo arrives at Luna City and soon discovers that not everything is as it seems. He </span>
  <span id="freeText13743896112304670658" style="display:none">Leo Gray is embarrassed by his behind the times parents who don’t see the need for anything high-tech. They own Minutes &amp; Widgets, a clock fixing shop, which isn’t doing so well in 2113 when most people rely on self-flying cars and robots that do all of the housework. Leo is an eleven year old science whiz who is hoping to secure a place at the Lunar Academy, located in a new city inside the moon called Luna City.<br /><br />Leo arrives at Luna City and soon discovers that not everything is as it seems. He and his new friends wind up trying to solve a mystery that has catastrophic implications.<br /><br />While I liked Leo, his friend Andromeda and the quirky conspiracy theorist Mr. Dawgspat I didn’t connect emotionally with any of the characters. I loved the diversity of the characters and the inclusion of a child with a prosthetic who is brilliant at sport, although when they get called <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[One-leg <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> by one of the mean kids it isn’t challenged. I enjoyed the descriptions of the way of life in 2113, particularly the contrasts between Leo’s old fashioned parents and everyone else.<br /><br />It seemed weird to me that after promising to make contact with his family daily while he’s at Luna City there was no mention of it after this, nor any indication that his family knew anything about <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[him being in a coma and missing the entire second semester of school as a result <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />There were a couple of times where I felt I missed something when the story jumped from one part of the narrative to the next and was disappointed that the big build up to the lunar eclipse essentially fizzled for me when Leo <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[missed it completely because he was in a coma <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. The story also wrapped up too quickly for my liking with Leo <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[waking from his coma, attending a sporting match straight away and then suddenly leaving all of his friends in Luna City <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br /><br />I really liked the illustrations at the beginning of each chapter. Younger readers may not miss the character development I was hoping for or be troubled by the unanswered questions. Overall it was a quick, enjoyable read but I don’t think it will be memorable long term for me. If you’re sensitive about the language your children are exposed to in books you may want to know that one of the characters has a peculiar little catchphrase - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[HOLE-E-CRAPPER-BAPPERS <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. The ending lends itself to a sequel.<br /><br />Thank you to NetGalley and Greenleaf Book Group for the opportunity to read this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13743896112304670658" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2803405431" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2803405431" />
    <a title="lemoncupcakes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/96654377-lemoncupcakes"><img alt="lemoncupcakes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556573313p2/96654377.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2803405431?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="lemoncupcakes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="lemoncupcakes" href="/user/show/96654377-lemoncupcakes">lemoncupcakes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2803405431" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15435592021872488334">This was a fast fun read! The author's writing style is really different. Instead of greeting us with a typical dystopian setting, we meet the main character in a present day setting within a futuristic setting, ex: Leo's family still watch tv and use a dishwasher even though robots now do everything and tvs no longer exist. This adds to the books humor, but there is also some mystery and conflict here as to why that is, which I suspect the author is holding back from us for a later installment.</span>
  <span id="freeText15435592021872488334" style="display:none">This was a fast fun read! The author's writing style is really different. Instead of greeting us with a typical dystopian setting, we meet the main character in a present day setting within a futuristic setting, ex: Leo's family still watch tv and use a dishwasher even though robots now do everything and tvs no longer exist. This adds to the books humor, but there is also some mystery and conflict here as to why that is, which I suspect the author is holding back from us for a later installment. <br /><br />There are a number of minor stories in this book as well, ex: trees are disappearing all over town and Leo’s neighbor (who’s the landscaping security guy) claims to have worked for the government and that his wife was abducted by aliens called Lunalings. This is another example of where the author leaves us to wonder about what’s really going on, as we only get the answer to where the trees went and why they disappeared. We don’t find out more about the alien abducted wife, which I was really curious about. <br /><br />The main story takes off when Leo leaves his sheltered home on Earth to attend the moon’s academy after winning a national science competition. At the academy Leo meets other kids who were awarded acceptance for various talents like math, history, theater, and music, though some did gain entrance from their rich parents. <br /><br />Low and behold, the selection of Earth’s most gifted comes with a Doom’s Day message for Earth: Melkorg invasion! An evil alien race that consumes time and erases life on planets are on track to attack ours. And Leo and his friends are now on a mission to stop them before their portal opens on the night of the lunar eclipse. Only a second internal plan to destroy the moon is soon revealed, and Leo ends up in a hospital bed with no way to better assist when he runs into it.<br /><br />In the end, we find out that eclipse hasn’t yet happened and that there is something more going on behind the office doors of the lunar president. Leo ultimately leaves the reader with an even bigger question in the end that shouts out: sequel!<br /><br />I'm really looking forward to seeing where this series will go! </span>
  <a data-text-id="15435592021872488334" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer280116023885898236">I won this book in a goodreads drawing.<br/><br/>Derivative juvenile about an 11 year old kid that wins a ticket to a city in the moon 100 years from now. I was constantly reminded of scenes from other, similar books, whether Charlie and the Chocolate Factory or Harry Potter.<br/><br/>Might float your boat.</span>

<div id="review_2834167613" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2834167613" />
    <a title="Christi M" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68535952-christi-m"><img alt="Christi M" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1575753449p2/68535952.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2834167613?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christi M" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christi M" href="/user/show/68535952-christi-m">Christi M</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68535952-christi-m?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68535952-christi-m?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2834167613" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11647273500312859385">What a fun read this book was! I won Leo Gray and the Lunar Eclipse in a GoodReads Giveaway and was excited to get it because it combined two genre's I enjoy: middle grade fiction and sci fi.<br/><br/>Leo Gray is the eldest child of two parents who are very 'unhip' and do not appreciate the modern things of year 2113 and instead identify more with "old" Earth. Mr. Gray, especially, is very hard on modern life and the government, so that when there is a chance for Leo to enter a government rocket-building </span>
  <span id="freeText11647273500312859385" style="display:none">What a fun read this book was! I won Leo Gray and the Lunar Eclipse in a GoodReads Giveaway and was excited to get it because it combined two genre's I enjoy: middle grade fiction and sci fi.<br /><br />Leo Gray is the eldest child of two parents who are very 'unhip' and do not appreciate the modern things of year 2113 and instead identify more with "old" Earth. Mr. Gray, especially, is very hard on modern life and the government, so that when there is a chance for Leo to enter a government rocket-building contest with the reward of getting a free ticket to go to school in Luna City (on the Moon), Leo's mom enters him in secretly. Leo does eventually get to Luna City, but not without a few hiccups along the way. Once there he then makes friends with kids from different countries who all have unique talents and together they discover that they must help save Earth and Luna City from those who wish to destroy both.<br /><br />I loved how fun and interesting this future Earth is. In this story, the future is one of hope and wonder and promising ideas that we currently only dream of. A city on the moon! Robots with personalities! Levitating chairs! Flying go-karts! Life in this future Earth isn't perfect - there are still bullies and still those with money and those who scrape by each month. So it was a real treat when Leo received his ticket and we were able to experience his trip first to space camp and then to the moon along with him.<br /><br />Although I did enjoy the overall story, there were a couple of parts that bothered me as a reader. The first was Mr. Gray, Leo's father, as he unilaterally makes some decisions without consulting his wife or thinking about how it might impact his son. In addition, I was really bothered about how he blamed his son for something that happened to a watch - not because Leo was anywhere near the watch because he was miles away - but because Mr. Gray blamed him for being distracted for a moment when the 'watch event' occurred. I thought both events sent the wrong message to a young reader; however, the book did hint that perhaps there is more to Mr. Gray than we were shown so I suspect that future books will show what was really going on with Mr. Gray.<br /><br />The only other item that concerned me was how long it took for Leo to recover from an event at the very end of the book. The recovery time seemed a bit on the extreme side, but also wrapped up the end of the school year a bit too neatly - like perhaps it was rushed. I would have liked for the story to have been a bit longer so that more could have been explored or drawn out, but here I speak as an adult all the while knowing that these books are written for a younger age than myself and therefore probably shouldn't be too long.<br /><br />All in all, I really enjoyed this book. I found it a lot of fun to read and enjoyed using my imagination and I believe kids will enjoy it too. <br /><br />Thank you to GoodReads, the author, and the publisher for this book and the opportunity to review it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11647273500312859385" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84662839-lynn?shelf=giveaways">giveaways</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2847486543" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13433230405342271343">I received Leo Gray and the Lunar Eclipse through a Goodreads Giveaway.<br/><br/>I'll start off by saying the cover of this book is adorable, and definitely helps to set the tone for the book. It's a cute read, and I could see it being a complete hit for children. I mean, what child isn't fascinated by aliens and robots? Or space travel? It's a book that hits all the necessary targets to make a great children's book that can also be enjoyed by adults. <br/><br/>Personally, my favorite aspect of Leo Gray and the Lun</span>
  <span id="freeText13433230405342271343" style="display:none">I received Leo Gray and the Lunar Eclipse through a Goodreads Giveaway.<br /><br />I'll start off by saying the cover of this book is adorable, and definitely helps to set the tone for the book. It's a cute read, and I could see it being a complete hit for children. I mean, what child isn't fascinated by aliens and robots? Or space travel? It's a book that hits all the necessary targets to make a great children's book that can also be enjoyed by adults. <br /><br />Personally, my favorite aspect of Leo Gray and the Lunar Eclipse was the contrast between the futuristic families who took full advantage of the technology offered to them and the Gray family who is completely engrossed in all things 2013 to the embarrassment of Leo Gray. I found myself laughing at how the other kids made fun of Leo over toilet paper, and how Mrs. Witz reacted upon entering Leo's home which contained a television. It was refreshing to see the future from the perspective of someone living in a family focused on our timeline, instead of their own. <br /><br />Overall Leo Gray and the Lunar Eclipse is a fun afternoon read that would be great for children interested in the future, and in space. I could see it being a nighttime favorite for a lot of children, and one of those books that they always demand to be reread.</span>

It has some great characters (especially Leo himself), some interesting animal pets and villainous aliens. I liked the way the contrast between the present and the future is presented. I think this is a good book that will engage the young reader.<br/>I won a copy of this book in a Goodreads giveaway for this honest review.</span>

<div id="review_2770245575" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2770245575" />
    <a title="Pammycats" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39659978-pammycats"><img alt="Pammycats" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

        <a title="Pammycats" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pammycats" href="/user/show/39659978-pammycats">Pammycats</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2770245575" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3489569700317285892">Leo Gray and the Lunar Eclipse<br/>By: K.L. Kruk<br/><br/>I received a free ARC of this book in exchange for my honest opinion.<br/><br/>I did really like this book. It has a great mystery at its core. It feels like the beginning of a very solid series of books. <br/><br/>Setting:<br/>The setting for this story is about 100 years in the future. The futuristic details are fantastic and abundant. They are just enough ahead of where we are to be believable. It was exciting and felt like the ideas were coming from a very free and happy br</span>
  <span id="freeText3489569700317285892" style="display:none">Leo Gray and the Lunar Eclipse<br />By: K.L. Kruk<br /><br />I received a free ARC of this book in exchange for my honest opinion.<br /><br />I did really like this book. It has a great mystery at its core. It feels like the beginning of a very solid series of books. <br /><br />Setting:<br />The setting for this story is about 100 years in the future. The futuristic details are fantastic and abundant. They are just enough ahead of where we are to be believable. It was exciting and felt like the ideas were coming from a very free and happy brain. Even the use of language is just altered enough to be definitely different but understandable. The language is breezy and light. I was mesmerized by this world.<br /><br />Characters<br />First, I have to just comment that “Leo Gray” in real life is the name of one of the original Tuskegee Airmen. I’m a flight nerd so I wondered if this was done on purpose or purely accidentally. We are told that Leo's eyes are the color of Mercury which is gray (his last name). These two things just felt like little space nuggets that the author was giving us.<br /><br />Okay, back to the characters ...<br />The story is told from Leo Gray’s (11 years old) perspective. Occasionally though, it shifts narrators. For instance, we hear the internal musings of Leo’s Dad as he contemplates his reasoning for distrusting government, etc. This helps the reader understand his character better but from a narrative standpoint, it is disconcerting to have this sort of shift of view. There is a mystery and the reader needs to follow the trail with Leo<br /><br />Speaking of Leo’s Dad, I had a hard time really understanding his character. At the beginning, he seems sort of eccentric but okay. As the story progresses, the book reveals him to be sort of a bully. The family can’t dig into the noodle casserole until Dad has the first helping. Dad unilaterally decides that Leo isn’t going to the Lunar Academy. Mom stands by helplessly, trying to connive and lie behind his back but unable to stand up to him bravely. Then, Dad blames Leo because someone stole something from the store while Dad was distracted. He then sells Leo’s ticket to the Lunar Academy to make up the money. Then, after Leo gets another ticket, Dad agrees to let him go and now we are supposed to see the more tender side to him as he says goodbye to Leo. Nope, I am not buying that at all.<br /><br />Speaking of that second ticket, how is that working? So, he gets a second ticket to Lunar City from Gudrun. First, why does Gudrun have this ticket? Secondly, is it a ticket to Lunar City or Space Camp? Thirdly, why, if it is a ticket to Lunar City, does Leo now have admittance to the school at Lunar City? Those two things don’t conflate.<br /><br />Another odd thing is that after Leo arrives at school, the reader doesn’t see or hear anything more about his family. The story is all about his friends. The friends are a bit predictable - smart girl, wise cracking but not too brainy roomy, true blue best friend - but I felt real affection for them. However, I think it was odd that we don’t see or hear from his family. Leo is basically in a coma for months. He has been involved in a serious event but no family.<br /><br />So, lots of complaints and lots of odd holes in this book. They were distracting to me and forced me out of the narrative stream. However, I liked the story enough to hope that the future of this series is better than this present book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3489569700317285892" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2963306484" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2963306484" />
    <a title="Amanda Sanders" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57128115-amanda-sanders"><img alt="Amanda Sanders" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2963306484?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda Sanders" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda Sanders" href="/user/show/57128115-amanda-sanders">Amanda Sanders</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2963306484" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4764695735713904213">This Sci Fi book tries to emulate Harry Potter but is totally unsuccessful in matching the quality. In the story, Leo enters a contest to attend a lunar academy against his father's wishes. After he wins, his father won't let him go. Instead Leo has to do manual labor for a company his father knows. This is at the age of 10. I hope our child labor laws do not disappear and allow something like this in the future. 10-year-olds can not work for any reputable businesses. After proving how hard-work</span>
  <span id="freeText4764695735713904213" style="display:none">This Sci Fi book tries to emulate Harry Potter but is totally unsuccessful in matching the quality. In the story, Leo enters a contest to attend a lunar academy against his father's wishes. After he wins, his father won't let him go. Instead Leo has to do manual labor for a company his father knows. This is at the age of 10. I hope our child labor laws do not disappear and allow something like this in the future. 10-year-olds can not work for any reputable businesses. After proving how hard-working he is, Leo is suddenly allowed to attend the lunar academy. His father was impressed with his work ethic. This change of heart came after Leo's dad sold the ticket to attend the academy for next to nothing so they had to use the new money earned to pay for it. The dad is stuck in the past and plays with old gadgets such as a TV. Apparently TVs are long gone, but they were able to get a random signal. This is scientifically inaccurate. The whole dad character development was weird. He was a total butthead but in the end I think the author wanted us to like him. Another scientific problem I had was the contest. There is obviously plenty of well developed space travel in this time and it is not something they need future scientists working on, but the contest was about designing rockets. That's like asking kids of today to design a TV instead of a robot. At one point a college educated character says "I done got me a college education." It was obnoxious. There are lots of baby talk and baby sounding terms in the story and it was way to cutesy wootsy. The author over uses caps. THERE IS YELLING WITH TEXT CAPS ON ALMOST EVERY PAGE. Over use of something that is supposed to show emphasis ruins the emphatic effect. One of the characters seems to be trying to be Hermione and the boarding school uses points for homework and classwork to help win a competition. None of that was original. I was never gripped with the plot because I was too annoyed with characters and background. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4764695735713904213" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6980938299344609070" style="display:none">Leo Gray and the Lunar Eclipse is a Science Fiction by the author KJ Kruk. Story is set in the future when the world has become Hi-Tech. Homes are now robotically maintained, there are self-flying cars and ozone protective clothing. But Gray family is still not modern. <br /><br />When Mrs Gray told Mr Gray about the Science competition in which the winner will get a free ticket to Lunar City, Mr Gray clearly mentioned that his family has nothing to do with that competition. But Mrs Gray supported her son and sent him to participate in the competition. Will Leo get an entry ticket to Lunar City? <br /><br />This is an intriguing story. While reading it, I didn't felt bored anytime. I loved every bit of this story. Language of the book is easy. Young readers will be able to understand the simple language and enjoy the story as Leo and his friends will take readers on great adventures. It's a great science fiction story that I strongly recommend to my friends. <br /><br />Rating 4.5/5</span>

<div id="review_2940244498" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2940244498" />
    <a title="Kathy Tang" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/101404599-kathy-tang"><img alt="Kathy Tang" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2940244498?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy Tang" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy Tang" href="/user/show/101404599-kathy-tang">Kathy Tang</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2940244498" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5044307137818426166">***I received this book for free in ebook format in exchange for an honest review*** Though I can't comment on the physical book, the ebook was fun to read and I loved the contrast between the main character's family and the futuristic world of 2113. Though I'm not normally a fan of sci-fi, this world wasn't obsessed with laser guns, space wars or aliens, and read more like a classic kid's fantasy book in a futuristic setting. Like another reviewer mentioned, it did a good job not being a "boys-</span>
  <span id="freeText5044307137818426166" style="display:none">***I received this book for free in ebook format in exchange for an honest review*** Though I can't comment on the physical book, the ebook was fun to read and I loved the contrast between the main character's family and the futuristic world of 2113. Though I'm not normally a fan of sci-fi, this world wasn't obsessed with laser guns, space wars or aliens, and read more like a classic kid's fantasy book in a futuristic setting. Like another reviewer mentioned, it did a good job not being a "boys-only" book or a "girls-only" book and has great diversity within the characters (and is inclusive of disabilities!). The only negative I really had with this book was 1) that it was ebook format which made it harder for me to read and 2) it did leave me with a lot of questions at the end that were not resolved from the begining, which I'm assuming we'll get the answers to in the next book of this new series. In short, I think this book's appeal is spot-on for middle graders and I look forward to sharing it with my classroom later this year.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5044307137818426166" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3635826100" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer182119786929343786">Leo Gray is an elder child of his parents. He loves to read books on science, physics and astronomy. Everyone in 2113 year lives in a robotically maintained homes but Leo's parents lives in a wooden paneled home. Leo was lucky that inspite of being poor, he got a chance to participate in first-ever National Junior Science Competition for free-entry to Luna City. <br/><br/>His Science teacher and he went for the competition in her van-jet. Leo's rocket launched incredibly at the competition that was held i</span>
  <span id="freeText182119786929343786" style="display:none">Leo Gray is an elder child of his parents. He loves to read books on science, physics and astronomy. Everyone in 2113 year lives in a robotically maintained homes but Leo's parents lives in a wooden paneled home. Leo was lucky that inspite of being poor, he got a chance to participate in first-ever National Junior Science Competition for free-entry to Luna City. <br /><br />His Science teacher and he went for the competition in her van-jet. Leo's rocket launched incredibly at the competition that was held in front of Times Square, New York and he came second. Why Leo didn't deserved the first position at the competition? Is Gavin, a rich participant better than Leo? Find out yourself by diving into the future with our protagonist Leo Gray. <br /><br />As the story moves forward, Leo has to take difficult decisions like saving Earth or saving the Lunar Eclipse. Author's vivid imagination will leave the readers awestruck. This is a wonderful story for middle grade readers. I have read many science fictions but this story is captivating. Story made me at laugh many times. It is a light story that will totally refresh your mood. Don't think twice and go ahead with it. It's a promising one.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3255044323998471406">Stories that captures my interest from the very first page are very rare. Leo Gray and the Lunar Eclipse is a science fiction set in the year 2113. It hooked me from the very first page. The way Leo's family is different from the other families made me laughed and I could feel how much embarrassed Leo must have been because of his parents especially his dad. Leo's science teacher Miss Witz at Saint Margaret’s Academy came to his home so she could get Leo to the competition where he has a chance </span>
  <span id="freeText3255044323998471406" style="display:none">Stories that captures my interest from the very first page are very rare. Leo Gray and the Lunar Eclipse is a science fiction set in the year 2113. It hooked me from the very first page. The way Leo's family is different from the other families made me laughed and I could feel how much embarrassed Leo must have been because of his parents especially his dad. Leo's science teacher Miss Witz at Saint Margaret’s Academy came to his home so she could get Leo to the competition where he has a chance to win a free ticket to Luna City. Leo went to the competition without his father's permission. Unfortunately, the competition was LIVE from Times Square and Leo's dad saw him on TV when he was in his clock shop. Leo won the competition because of his amazing shuttle entry RX-10 and finally made to the Lunar City. This is the first time I have read a fiction where a young boy has went to moon. World building is amazing. Plot is gripping making it an unputdownable book. Writing style of the author is fantastic. Little illustrations along with each chapter name looks very nice. Cover of the book is eye catchy. The story is set in a futuristic world with robotic technologies. A page turner<br /><br />Rating 4.5/5</span>
  <a data-text-id="3255044323998471406" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('t7LqcA5fOVvRDUfxu7gsA9tB9D+JRZcyGqBtrMTeufqP/Fe/ELKUAwdxpSkFAnzk/0OTVeTTQ9ekPZ89wmeGtA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wNk9PL/QrszcdlY67mvr6leVYco+sWcc5betiCS1SCj4l4DzoT0DlAoKtOJQ0bsNc5cGoFMns/lbKl8ZIgx3Zg==')})
  }
//]]>
